<p><b>Memphis Depay</b> (<small>Dutch pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[mmfs dpi]</a></span>; born 13 February 1994), also known simply as <b>Memphis</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-things_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-things-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is a Dutch professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a>  who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> club <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a>.
</p><p>Depay began his professional career with <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a>, where, under the influence of manager <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Cocu" title="Phillip Cocu">Phillip Cocu</a>, he became an integral part of the team, scoring 50 goals in 124 games across all competitions. During the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Eredivisie#Top_scorers" title="2014–15 Eredivisie">2014–15 season</a>, he was the <a href="/wiki/Eredivisie" title="Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a>'s top scorer with 22 goals in 30 games, and helped the team win the Eredivisie title for the first time since 2008. He also won the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Footballer_of_the_Year#Dutch_Football_Talent_of_the_Year" title="Dutch Footballer of the Year">Dutch Footballer of the Year</a> for his performances during the season. His performances also led him to be named the "Best Young Player" in the world in 2015 by <i><a href="/wiki/France_Football" title="France Football">France Football</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-France_Football_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France_Football-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Depay joined English side <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in June 2015 for a reported fee of £25&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> After a disappointing spell there, he joined French club Lyon in January 2017.
</p><p>A product of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Football_Association" title="Royal Dutch Football Association">Royal Dutch Football Association</a> (KNVB) institution, Depay has represented the national team at every professional level from early developmental stages under the tutelage of iconic Dutch coaches and players alike. He was part of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_under-17_football_team" title="Netherlands national under-17 football team">Netherlands Under-17 team</a> which won the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_European_Under-17_Championship" title="2011 UEFA European Under-17 Championship">2011 European Championship</a>. He made his senior debut in 2013 and the following year was part of their squad that came third at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>, where he made his breakthrough performances on the international stage. More recently, he was a member of the national setup for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a> qualification campaign. 
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PSV">PSV</span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Moordrecht" title="Moordrecht">Moordrecht</a>, Depay impressed football scouts from <a href="/wiki/Sparta_Rotterdam" title="Sparta Rotterdam">Sparta Rotterdam</a> at the age of eight on the fields of his boyhood club vv Moordrecht. It took only three seasons before scouts from Sparta snatched Depay from his local club. Club chairman Ton Redegeld said, "Memphis was as a young player already complete. He was two-footed and strong. If we won 7–0, he scored five times and would assist two times".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> When he turned 12, Depay caught the eye of clubs such as <a href="/wiki/AFC_Ajax" title="AFC Ajax">Ajax</a>, <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a>. His grandfather, despite being an Ajax fan himself, advised Depay to move to PSV.<sup id="cite_ref-Ramesh_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ramesh-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2011.E2.80.9313:_Beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–13:_Beginnings">2011–13: Beginnings</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Depay_PSV_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Depay_PSV_2011.jpg/170px-Depay_PSV_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Depay_PSV_2011.jpg/255px-Depay_PSV_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Depay_PSV_2011.jpg/340px-Depay_PSV_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="374" data-file-height="666" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Depay_PSV_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depay with PSV in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In 2011, Depay was on trial for PSV's first team while playing for <a href="/wiki/Jong_PSV" title="Jong PSV">Jong PSV</a>, the club's reserve team. He made his official debut on 21 September 2011 in a <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_KNVB_Cup" title="2011–12 KNVB Cup">KNVB Cup second round match</a> against amateur side <a href="/wiki/VVSB" title="VVSB">VVSB</a>, opening an 8–0 away win.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> His first Eredivisie match was 26 February 2012, when PSV beat rivals Feyenoord 3–2<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="seems like a ludicrously lopsided score line...check for vandalism? (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> at the <a href="/wiki/Philips_Stadion" title="Philips Stadion">Philips Stadion</a>, coming on in added time for <a href="/wiki/Zakaria_Labyad" title="Zakaria Labyad">Zakaria Labyad</a>. On 18 March, six minutes after replacing <a href="/wiki/Dries_Mertens" title="Dries Mertens">Dries Mertens</a>, he scored his first league goal to confirm a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/SC_Heerenveen" title="SC Heerenveen">Heerenveen</a>. He made a total of eight league appearances in his first season, all as a substitute, scoring three goals.
</p><p>Depay featured in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Football_Association" title="Royal Dutch Football Association">KNVB</a> Cup Final on 8 April, playing the final four minutes of the 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Heracles_Almelo" title="Heracles Almelo">Heracles</a> in place of Mertens at <a href="/wiki/De_Kuip" title="De Kuip">De Kuip</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> under interim coach <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Cocu" title="Phillip Cocu">Phillip Cocu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-test_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> On 29 June 2012, Depay signed his first professional contract with PSV, tying himself to the <i>Boeren</i> until 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 August, Depay featured in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Johan_Cruyff_Shield" title="2012 Johan Cruyff Shield">2012 Johan Cruyff Shield</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Arena">Amsterdam Arena</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Narsingh" title="Luciano Narsingh">Luciano Narsingh</a> for the final six minutes as PSV defeated league champions Ajax 4–2. He made 20 Eredivisie appearances in his second season, scoring twice, including two starts. The first of these was on 2 March 2013 in a 2–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/VVV-Venlo" title="VVV-Venlo">VVV-Venlo</a>, scoring after three minutes after being set up by fellow teenager <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Locadia" title="Jürgen Locadia">Jürgen Locadia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> PSV again reached the cup final, losing 1–2 to <a href="/wiki/AZ_Alkmaar" title="AZ Alkmaar">AZ</a> on 9 May, with Depay playing five minutes in place of Mertens.
</p>
<h4><span id="2013.E2.80.9314:_Breakthrough_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013–14:_Breakthrough_season">2013–14: Breakthrough season</span></h4>
<p>Depay scored his first goal in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European football</a> on 30 July 2013, when he drifted in from the left and then smashed the ball into the top corner past goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Bossut" title="Sammy Bossut">Sammy Bossut</a> as PSV defeated <a href="/wiki/Zulte_Waregem" class="mw-redirect" title="Zulte Waregem">Zulte Waregem</a> 2–0 in the first leg of their <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round#First_leg_3" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League qualifying phase and play-off round">UEFA Champions League</a> third qualifying round tie.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> PSV failed to qualify for the group stage of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> but in its second group stage match in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>, Depay scored again, this time curling the ball into the net from outside the area, as the Dutch side defeated <a href="/wiki/FC_Chornomorets_Odesa" title="FC Chornomorets Odesa">Chornomorets Odesa</a> 2–0 on 3 October.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay provided the assist for <a href="/wiki/Tim_Matav%C5%BE" title="Tim Matavž">Tim Matavž</a>'s goal against <a href="/wiki/Roda_JC_Kerkrade" title="Roda JC Kerkrade">Roda JC</a> on 27 October 2013, but picked up two second-half yellow cards and was sent off for the first time in his professional career as PSV slumped to a 2–1 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On 15 December, Depay helped PSV to just their second win in 13 matches, scoring twice in a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Utrecht" title="FC Utrecht">Utrecht</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Depay helped PSV rack up their eighth win a row on 23 March 2014, a 3–1 win over Roda JC, having a hand in <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Ruiz" title="Bryan Ruiz">Bryan Ruiz</a>'s game-winning goal despite wearing a protective mask to cover a bruised eye socket suffered in a challenge with <a href="/wiki/Renato_Ibarra" title="Renato Ibarra">Renato Ibarra</a> of <a href="/wiki/SBV_Vitesse" title="SBV Vitesse">Vitesse</a> on 15 March.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay helped PSV secure a place in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_competitions#For_clubs" title="UEFA competitions">European competition</a> for the 41st consecutive year, edging the ball past goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jelle_ten_Rouwelaar" title="Jelle ten Rouwelaar">Jelle ten Rouwelaar</a> to score their first in a 2–0 win against <a href="/wiki/NAC_Breda" title="NAC Breda">NAC Breda</a>; the final day win ensured that the club would finish fourth in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Eredivisie" title="2013–14 Eredivisie">Eredivisie</a> table.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315:_Top_scorer_and_league_title"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15:_Top_scorer_and_league_title">2014–15: Top scorer and league title</span></h4>
<p>After a successful showing at the 2014 World Cup, Depay was linked to a number of clubs, including <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Amid the speculation surrounding his future, he started the season for PSV in impressive fashion. Depay came off the bench to score one goal and deliver one assist in the return game of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Europa_League#Third_Qualifying_Round" title="2014–15 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> third qualifying round tie between PSV and <a href="/wiki/SKN_St._P%C3%B6lten" title="SKN St. Pölten">SKN St. Pölten</a> on 7 August, as his team progressed to the play-off round after a 3–2 away win, giving them a 4–2 aggregate win over the Austrians.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In the opening game of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Eredivisie" title="2014–15 Eredivisie">Eredivisie season</a> three days later, Depay played a major part in PSV's 3–1 away win against promoted side <a href="/wiki/Willem_II_(football_club)" title="Willem II (football club)">Willem II</a> by scoring two goals.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He improved on this performance in the following game, scoring two free-kicks and delivering the assist for <a href="/wiki/Georginio_Wijnaldum" title="Georginio Wijnaldum">Georginio Wijnaldum</a>'s goal in a convincing 6–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/NAC_Breda" title="NAC Breda">NAC Breda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 28 August, in the Europa League play-off second leg away in Belarus, he scored two late goals against <a href="/wiki/FC_Shakhtyor_Soligorsk" title="FC Shakhtyor Soligorsk">Shakhtyor Soligorsk</a> as PSV won 3–0 on aggregate to reach the group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Depay then suffered a groin injury during PSV's 3–1 defeat at <a href="/wiki/PEC_Zwolle" title="PEC Zwolle">PEC Zwolle</a> on 13 September and he was substituted in the 18th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 April 2015, Depay scored PSV's second goal with a free-kick from 35 yards out in a 4–1 home win over Heerenveen to give PSV its 22nd Eredivisie title, its first since 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, the club confirmed that they had received interest from others wishing to sign him, including Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He scored his last home goal for PSV in a 2–0 win against Heracles on 10 May. As he was substituted off, the stadium was filled with a deafening cheer from the crowd around him and he was met with numerous congratulations from his teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season as the league's top scorer with 22 goals, two ahead of runner-up and teammate <a href="/wiki/Luuk_de_Jong" title="Luuk de Jong">Luuk de Jong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-top_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfer_and_pre-season">Transfer and pre-season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg/220px-Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg/330px-Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg/440px-Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1438" data-file-height="1684" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memphis_Depay_-_July_2015c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depay playing for United in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Depay had originally been the subject of several bids by English side <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, with club manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> eventually going on to turn down a move for him altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
On 7 May 2015, PSV confirmed that they had agreed a deal with Manchester United over Depay's transfer, subject to a medical.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> United manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> said that he was "forced" into signing him early, due to interest from <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Despite insistence from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Rodgers" title="Brendan Rodgers">Brendan Rodgers</a> that he had never been after Depay, PSV director Marcel Brands had stated that he had conversations with Liverpool over a possible signing.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 12 June 2015, United confirmed the signing of Depay, for a reported fee of £25&#160;million on a four-year contract with the option to extend for a further year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He was unveiled as a Manchester United player at a press conference on 10 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> This made him the fourth player to join United from PSV after <a href="/wiki/Jaap_Stam" title="Jaap Stam">Jaap Stam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Park_Ji-sung" title="Park Ji-sung">Park Ji-sung</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a>.
</p><p>Depay made his United debut in a pre-season friendly against <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">Club América</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> on 17 July, contesting the first half as United fielded a different 11 players for each 45 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for the club four days later during a 3–1 win over the <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_Earthquakes" title="San Jose Earthquakes">San Jose Earthquakes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> At his own request, Depay was given the iconic number 7 shirt – previously worn by club legends such as <a href="/wiki/George_Best" title="George Best">George Best</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Robson" title="Bryan Robson">Bryan Robson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Cantona" title="Eric Cantona">Eric Cantona</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> – after the departure of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Di_Mar%C3%ADa" title="Ángel Di María">Ángel Di María</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season">2015–16 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cskamu_52.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cskamu_52.jpg/220px-Cskamu_52.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="325" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Cskamu_52.jpg/330px-Cskamu_52.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/Cskamu_52.jpg 2x" data-file-width="345" data-file-height="509" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cskamu_52.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depay during a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Depay made his <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> debut on 8 August as the season opened with a 1–0 victory over Tottenham Hotspur at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>. He was substituted after 68 minutes for <a href="/wiki/Ander_Herrera" title="Ander Herrera">Ander Herrera</a>, and Van Gaal said after the match that Depay was playing in too eager a manner.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On 18 August, Depay scored his first two goals for Manchester United, and assisted <a href="/wiki/Maroune_Fellaini" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroune Fellaini">Maroune Fellaini</a>'s final goal, in a 3–1 home victory over <a href="/wiki/Club_Brugge_KV" title="Club Brugge KV">Club Brugge</a> in the first leg of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League qualifying phase and play-off round">Champions League play-offs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League qualifying phase and play-off round">second leg</a>, Depay provided the assist for the first of <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a>'s three goals. He scored again on 15 September in the first game of the competition's <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a>, in an eventual 2–1 loss at his former team PSV.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Depay was labelled as United's "European Danger Man" following his early success in the Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Depay scored his first Premier League goal on 26 September, opening a 3–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, a victory that put United on top of the league for the first time in 110 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following his early struggles in the Premier League, Depay told Dutch newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/De_Telegraaf" title="De Telegraaf">De Telegraaf</a></i>, "There are a lot of games in Manchester. There are very few rest days and on training days you are mainly concerned with recovering. It's heavy, two games a week, always at a high level, and my body has to get used to that." These claims were dismissed by assistant manager and former United player <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>, who blamed Depay's flashy lifestyle for his poor form.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Regarding his form, Van Gaal warned Depay of not emulating Ángel Di María, who suffered a similar setback after joining United, and left prior to Depay's arrival.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Depay was later dropped to the bench, along with club and national teammate <a href="/wiki/Daley_Blind" title="Daley Blind">Daley Blind</a>, during United's 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on 17 October 2015, following the Netherlands' failure to qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, Depay was named in the 59-man longlist for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d&#39;Or">FIFA Ballon d'Or</a>, but did not make the shortlist.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After being dropped in four consecutive matches, Depay got his first start as a second striker due to <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Martial" title="Anthony Martial">Anthony Martial</a> and Wayne Rooney's unavailability, and seized the opportunity with his second league goal in a 2–1 away win over <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> at <a href="/wiki/Vicarage_Road" title="Vicarage Road">Vicarage Road</a>. He scored an 11th-minute opener when he volleyed in Ander Herrera's cross with his left foot. His performance earned Depay praise from van Gaal, as well as his first Premier League Man of the Match honor.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In a January 2016 match against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, Depay came on as a late substitute. Three minutes after coming on, Depay gave away the ball with a misplaced pass deep in Chelsea territory, then failed to track back properly as Chelsea scored from the counterattack in stoppage time to earn a draw.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay followed this with a goal each in United's <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League">two Europa League matches</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Midtjylland" title="FC Midtjylland">Midtjylland</a> in February. He scored United's solitary goal in 1–2 loss in the away leg then scored the final goal in a 5–1 win at home, allowing United to win 6–3 on aggregate. He also nutmegged Midtjylland defender <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_R%C3%B8mer" title="André Rømer">André Rømer</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Rabona" title="Rabona">rabona</a> in the home leg. Depay was lauded for his performance in the home leg, where he not only scored but also set up the first goal, earned his side two penalties and delivered a cross that led to an own goal. Rømer later said, "I've never been so close to crying after a match as I was today. Memphis is the best player I have ever faced. He is the best. He can do anything." Manager Louis van Gaal hailed the match as a "turning point" for Depay.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season">2016–17 season</span></h4>
<p>Depay made only four appearances (all of them as a substitute) and had a total playing time of just 20 minutes in the Premier League during the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">2016–17 season</a>. He only started one match in the 2016–17 season – the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EFL_Cup" title="2016–17 EFL Cup">EFL Cup</a> third round 3–1 away win over League One club <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a> on 21 September 2016 – and was substituted after playing 55 minutes of that match. After that match against Northampton Town, he only had 46 minutes of total playing time in competitive matches for Manchester United during the remainder of the 2016–17 season. Depay's last competitive match for Manchester United was on 24 November 2016 when he played the final eight minutes of a 4–0 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Europa_League_group_stage" title="2016–17 UEFA Europa League group stage">Europa League</a> home victory against <a href="/wiki/Feyenoord" title="Feyenoord">Feyenoord</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyon">Lyon</span></h3>
<p>On 20 January 2017, Depay signed a four-and-a-half-year deal with French club <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Olympique Lyonnais</a> which would tie him to the French club until the summer of 2021. This transfer is known as the first 'laptop transfer' in football as Depay chose his next destination with help from computer modelling by data intelligence company <a href="/wiki/SciSports" title="SciSports">SciSports</a>. The initial transfer fee was estimated to be £16–17&#160;million, potentially rising to £22&#160;million with the add-ons including Lyon qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> and Depay earning a new contract. The terms of the deal also included buy-back and sell-on clauses for Manchester United.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 January 2017, Depay made his competitive debut for Lyon by coming on as substitute for <a href="/wiki/Mathieu_Valbuena" title="Mathieu Valbuena">Mathieu Valbuena</a> in the 79th minute in a home <a href="/wiki/Ligue_1" title="Ligue 1">Ligue 1</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Olympique de Marseille</a>, which Lyon won 3–1.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Six days later, he made his first competitive start for Lyon in a home Ligue 1 match against <a href="/wiki/Lille_OSC" title="Lille OSC">Lille OSC</a>, almost scored when he smashed a shot just over the bar in the ninth minute and was substituted in the 68th minute by <a href="/wiki/Maxwel_Cornet" title="Maxwel Cornet">Maxwel Cornet</a>; Lyon lost the match 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 March 2017 in a game against <a href="/wiki/Toulouse_FC" title="Toulouse FC">Toulouse</a>, Depay scored a goal from nearly the halfway line. Depay later said it was "the goal of my life", although he also distanced himself from comparisons to Beckham's famous halfway line goal against Wimbledon in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the final day of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Ligue_1" title="2017–18 Ligue 1">2017–18 season</a>, Depay scored a hat-trick against <a href="/wiki/OGC_Nice" title="OGC Nice">Nice</a> as Lyon won 3–2 and qualified for the next season's UEFA Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 November 2019, Depay scored his fourth goal in as many games for Lyon against <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a> in a 3–1 win in the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2019–20 UEFA Champions League">2019–20 UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 10 December, he scored an equaliser against <a href="/wiki/RB_Leipzig" title="RB Leipzig">RB Leipzig</a> in a 2–2 draw to help Lyon to qualify to the knockout phase, hence he scored his 5th goal in 5 consecutive matches in the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 December, Depay tore his anterior cruciate ligament while playing against Rennes in Ligue 1, ending a successful season during which he had scored nine goals in 12 league starts for Lyon.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He returned from his injury to start for Lyon in the French League Cup final against <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain</a> on 31 July 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 7 August 2020, Depay scored in his sixth consecutive Champions League match, converting a penalty in a 2–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the second leg of their round of 16 tie; he is only the second Dutch player to score in six straight Champions League games, following fellow former Manchester United striker <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a>. The tie finished 2–2 on aggregate, but Lyon progressed on the away goals rule.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Lyon eventually reached the semi-finals for the second time in their history after 2010.
</p><p>On 28 August 2020, Depay scored a hat-trick in a 4–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Dijon_FCO" title="Dijon FCO">Dijon</a>, in the first match of the 2020–21 season.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span></h3>
<p>Depay was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_under-17_football_team" title="Netherlands national under-17 football team">Netherlands under-17 team</a> which won the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_European_Under-17_Championship" title="2011 UEFA European Under-17 Championship">2011 European Championship</a> in Serbia. In the final against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_under-17_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Germany national under-17 football team">Germany</a> in <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">Novi Sad</a>, he scored the goal which put the Netherlands ahead as they came from behind to defeat <a href="/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93Netherlands_football_rivalry" title="Germany–Netherlands football rivalry">their rivals</a> 5–2.<sup id="cite_ref-under_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-under-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, he participated in the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_U-17_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA U-17 World Cup">2011 FIFA U-17 World Cup</a> held in Mexico.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior">Senior</span></h3>
<p>Depay made his international debut on 15 October 2013, coming on for <a href="/wiki/Jeremain_Lens" title="Jeremain Lens">Jeremain Lens</a> in the last minute of a 2–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> at the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9E%C3%BCkr%C3%BC_Saraco%C4%9Flu_Stadium" title="ükrü Saracolu Stadium">ükrü Saracolu Stadium</a> in World Cup qualification.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay was selected by Netherlands manager Louis van Gaal in the final 23-man squad for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He came on as a substitute before the half-time whistle in the second group match against <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_soccer_team" title="Australia national soccer team">Australia</a> to replace defender <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Martins_Indi" title="Bruno Martins Indi">Bruno Martins Indi</a>, who had sustained a head injury, and in the 68th minute he scored the winning goal, a swerving effort from outside the box. He also set up <a href="/wiki/Robin_van_Persie" title="Robin van Persie">Robin van Persie</a>'s equaliser.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> He became the youngest Dutchman to score a goal at the World Cup, at the age of 20 years and four months.<sup id="cite_ref-test2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test2-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> He came on as a substitute again in the final group match against <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chile</a> on 23 June in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a> and scored the second goal for the Dutch, tapping in an <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a> cross, as they clinched first place with a 2–0 victory.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg/220px-Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg/330px-Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg/440px-Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2160" data-file-height="1438" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Depay_NL_Training_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depay training with the Netherlands in March 2015</div></div></div>
<p>On 11 July, Depay was named on the three-man shortlist for the tournament's <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup#Awards" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">Best Young Player</a> award, together with Frenchmen <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pogba" title="Paul Pogba">Paul Pogba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rapha%C3%ABl_Varane" title="Raphaël Varane">Raphaël Varane</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> but lost out to Pogba.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay's first goal since the World Cup came in a friendly at the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Arena">Amsterdam Arena</a> on 5 June 2015, deflecting <a href="/wiki/Klaas-Jan_Huntelaar" title="Klaas-Jan Huntelaar">Klaas-Jan Huntelaar</a>'s shot to put the Netherlands 3–1 up against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a>, although the team eventually lost 4–3.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In October of that year, he was involved in a fight with teammate Robin van Persie at an international training camp; manager <a href="/wiki/Danny_Blind" title="Danny Blind">Danny Blind</a> stated to the media, "There are sometimes situations in training where players think different. Then you talk about it. That's what happened and then it's over."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The following month, both Depay and Van Persie were dropped from the Dutch squad for friendlies against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, with Blind stating of Depay, "In football you must function in a team. He doesn't always do that. That's something he has to learn."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memphis_Depay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Memphis_Depay.jpg/220px-Memphis_Depay.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Memphis_Depay.jpg/330px-Memphis_Depay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Memphis_Depay.jpg/440px-Memphis_Depay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1622" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memphis_Depay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depay playing for PSV in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>Early in his career, a PSV coach noted Depay as "very angry", and he now uses a <a href="/wiki/Life_coach" class="mw-redirect" title="Life coach">life coach</a> to aid his mentality.<sup id="cite_ref-things_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-things-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In April 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> described Depay as "a fearsome striker of the ball with his right foot but is usually used as an <a href="/wiki/Inverted_Winger" class="mw-redirect" title="Inverted Winger">inverted left winger</a> who cuts onto his right foot. A pacey and tricky player, his direct running makes him a difficult opponent for defenders".<sup id="cite_ref-things_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-things-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> However, they criticised him as "a ball-hog", pointing out his high rate of shots in comparison to a low rate of assists.<sup id="cite_ref-things_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-things-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Depay is also known for his <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Direct free kick">free-kick ability</a>. During the 2014–15 season, he was statistically the best set-piece taker in the whole of Europe, as he scored 7 times in 33 attempts, the most in all European leagues and the second-best accuracy.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former Dutch international and Dutch national team manager <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a> regards Depay as "a great talent", but says that he must continue his personal development due to the physicality and mental strength needed in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> defender <a href="/wiki/Arjan_de_Zeeuw" title="Arjan de Zeeuw">Arjan de Zeeuw</a> stated about Depay, "People regard him as a little bit arrogant, a little bit cocky, but I think he is a very good player, a very promising player, a very strong, very quick player and he's got some skill."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Depay has been compared to former United player <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> and fellow international <a href="/wiki/Arjen_Robben" title="Arjen Robben">Arjen Robben</a>. Thijs Slegers said about the comparisons, "Memphis is a little bit like Cristiano; they have similar qualities, although there are of course areas where Memphis is inferior. However, his determination to be the best is where I see the real similarity with Cristiano."<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Like Ronaldo, Depay combines technical expertise with pure physical strength.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Memphis_Depay&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Memphis+Depay%22">"Memphis Depay"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Memphis+Depay%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Memphis+Depay%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Memphis+Depay%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Memphis+Depay%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Memphis+Depay%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2021</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Depay began pursuing a hip-hop career in June 2017 when he released his <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>-inspired freestyle, "LA Vibes". The music video featured <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Promes" title="Quincy Promes">Quincy Promes</a>, Depay's teammate at the Netherlands national team. The song's music video earned around 150,000 views within hours of being uploaded to <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In December 2017, Depay released his freestyle track "Kings &amp; Queens". On 3 October 2018, he collaborated with musical artists <a href="/wiki/Winne" title="Winne">Winne</a> and Nana Fofie and producer Rass King for his Ghana-inspired single, "AKWAABA",<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and also released his third freestyle, "Porto Cervo (Interlude)", with Winne. Depay released his fourth freestyle, "5-mill" in response to his <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> account reaching 5&#160;million followers. Critics of the freestyle claimed that Depay's public image was hampered through his cigar-smoking and his careless attitude.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In December 2018, he released his second single, "No Love", over his cancelled engagement with model Lori Harvey. The song is multilingual, switching back and forth between <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In July 2019, Depay released "Fall Back".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 1 November 2019, <a href="/wiki/Broederliefde" title="Broederliefde">Broederliefde</a> released an album, <i>Broeders</i>, which featured Depay on the song "Lange Jas".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Depay recently announced his new song "For a Week" on his Instagram. On 17 April 2020, Memphis released "Dubai Freestyle". In September 2020, Memphis released his new song "2 Corinthians 5:7". On 27 November 2020, Memphis released his debut album <i>Heavy Stepper</i>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Depay was born in 1994 to a Ghanaian father, Dennis Depay, and a Dutch mother, Cora Schensema, in the small <a href="/wiki/South_Holland" title="South Holland">South Holland</a> village of <a href="/wiki/Moordrecht" title="Moordrecht">Moordrecht</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-depay1_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-depay1-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> It was not long, however, before the relationship between the two parents began to fall apart and when Depay was four, his father walked out on the family. Depay has numerous tattoos, including one on his left arm that is a tribute to his grandfather, who died on the day before he turned 15.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> When he scored against Australia in the 2014 World Cup, he kissed this tattoo and pointed to the sky, dedicating his goal to his late grandfather a moment which he then in 2016 commemorated with a tattoo on his left torso depicting <a href="/wiki/Christ_the_Redeemer_(statue)" title="Christ the Redeemer (statue)">Christ the Redeemer</a> and the date 18.06.14, referring to his first international goal for the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> He also has a tattoo on the inside of his lip stating <i>succesvol</i><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> which is Dutch for 'successful' and also has the words 'dream chaser' emblazoned on his upper torso.<sup id="cite_ref-things_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-things-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, it was announced on social media that Depay was engaged to Lori Harvey, the youngest daughter of American television personality <a href="/wiki/Steve_Harvey" title="Steve Harvey">Steve Harvey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Since then, they have ended their engagement and relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2020, Depay was criticised by several animal rights organisations for posting pictures of himself with a <a href="/wiki/Liger" title="Liger">liger</a> cub while on vacation in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>. Depay responded by stating that "ligers are not even wild animals".<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span></h3>
